## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator problem where acceleration (dv_dt) depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t. The relationship encodes Newton's second law with nonlinear restoring forces, damping, and potential external driving.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (undriven): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (harmonic external driving)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing equation)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (asymmetric restoring force)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-varying stiffness)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (nonlinear drag)
- Cubic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (nonlinear velocity-dependent damping)
- Mixed nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * x**2 * v (cross-coupled nonlinearity)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (amplitude-dependent frequency)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) indicate symmetric potential wells, while even powers (x**2) indicate asymmetric potentials
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v represent energy dissipation or injection (damping/anti-damping)
- Terms like (1 - c*x**2)*v indicate amplitude-dependent damping that switches sign, characteristic of self-sustained oscillations (limit cycles)
- Explicit time dependence through sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicates external periodic forcing, which can lead to chaos in nonlinear systems
- Product terms x**n * v represent coupling between position-dependent forces and velocity, often arising from nonlinear friction or geometric nonlinearity
- Negative coefficient on x (restoring) combined with positive x**3 coefficient indicates a hardening spring; reversed signs indicate softening
- If acceleration depends only on x and v (not t), the system is autonomous and can be fully analyzed in phase space (x, v)
- Parametric terms like x*cos(c*t) arise when system parameters oscillate in time, leading to parametric resonance phenomena

**GT:** `-0.0883678*v**3 - 0.195934*v*sin(x) - 3.99766*x**3 - 0.195934*sin(v)`

The GT has four terms:
1. `c*x**3` (polynomial)
2. `c*v**3` (polynomial)
3. `c*v*sin(x)` (transcendental - product of v and sin(x))
4. `c*sin(v)` (transcendental - sin of v)

The key challenge is that the GT contains `sin(x)` multiplied by `v` and `sin(v)`. Most candidates only have polynomial terms in x and v, so they cannot produce `sin(x)` or `sin(v)` terms.

Let me scan for candidates containing `sin` or other transcendental functions:

- **Candidates 5, 6, 9**: contain `sin(c*v + c)` terms
- **Candidate 16**: contains `log(c*v + 1)`
- **Candidate 17**: contains `log(c*v + 1)`

**Candidate 5:** `c0*x**3 + c1*v + c2*sin(c3*v + c4) + c5*v**3 + c6*v**5 + c7*v*x + c8*v*(c9 + x)**3`

**Candidate 6:** `c0*x**3 + c1*v + c2*sin(c3*v + c4) + c5*v**5 + c6*v*x + c7*v*(c8 + x)**3`

Same issue - has `sin(v)` but no `v*sin(x)`. **No match.**

**Candidate 9:** `c0*x**3 + c1*v + c2*sin(c3*v + c4) + c5*v**3 + c6*v**5 + c7*v*x + c8*v*x**3`

Has `sin(c3*v+c4)` which gives `sin(v)`, but no `v*sin(x)`. **No match.**

Now let me check all other candidates. They are all polynomial/power-law expressions in x, v, t (with some logs). None of them can produce both `v*sin(x)` and `sin(v)` terms.

Candidates with `v**c` (power with free exponent): 13, 14, 15, 48, 49, 50. These can't produce `sin` functions either.

Candidates with `log`: 16, 17. These can't produce `sin` functions.

Candidates with `sqrt`: 44. Can't produce `sin`.

**None of the candidates contain both a `sin(v)` term and a `v*sin(x)` term.** The GT fundamentally requires two different transcendental functions - `sin(v)` and `v*sin(x)` - and no candidate has the structural capability to produce both.

Even the candidates with `sin` (5, 6, 9) only have `sin` as a function of `v` (i.e., `sin(c*v+c)`), never as a function of `x`. There is no way to generate `v*sin(x)` from any of these candidates.

Therefore, no candidate can match the GT.

**Candidates without any sin/log/transcendental functions (purely polynomial):**

The GT contains `sin(x)` and `sin(v)` terms. No polynomial combination can exactly equal `sin(x)` or `sin(v)` for all x, v. So all purely polynomial candidates are **NO MATCH**.

Let me check which candidates have transcendental functions:

- **Candidate 5:** Has `sin(c3*v + c4)` - only sin of v, not sin of x). Missing `v*sin(x)`.
- **Candidate 6:** Has `sin(c3*v + c4)` - same issue.
- **Candidate 9:** Has `sin(c3*v + c4)` - same issue.
- **Candidate 16:** Has `log(c6*v + 1)` - log, not sin.
- **Candidate 17:** Has `log(c4*v + 1)` - log, not sin.
- **Candidate 44:** Has `sqrt(c3 + x)` - not sin.
- **Candidate 47-50:** Various rational/power forms, no sin(x).

None of the candidates contain both `sin(v)` and `sin(x)` (or equivalently `v*sin(x)`). In fact, none contain `sin(x)` at all.

The GT requires a `v*sin(x)` term which is linearly independent from all polynomial terms in x and v. No candidate has any function of `sin(x)`. Therefore, no candidate can match.

Let me double-check candidates 5, 6, 9 more carefully since they have sin terms:

**Candidate 5:** `c0*x┬│ + c1*v + c2*sin(c3*v + c4) + c5*v┬│ + c6*vŌüĄ + c7*v*x + c8*v*(c9+x)┬│`
This has `sin(c3*v+c4)` which can represent `sin(v)` but NOT `v*sin(x)`. Missing `v*sin(x)`. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidate 6:** Similar - has `sin(c3*v+c4)` but no `sin(x)`. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidate 9:** Same issue. **NO MATCH**.

All candidates fail because none contain `sin(x)` or any trigonometric function of x.
